<question>



Approximately how much does a big bag of Reese's Peanut Butter Cup Miniatures cost?



I recently moved from the USA to Australia, and unfortunately, we can't get Reese's products here.  I was contemplating asking a friend of mine if he could send some out if I pay for them and postage, but was wondering how many bags to ask him for.  Could someone give me an idea of how much the Miniatures cost, along with Reese's Pieces and various other Reese's products?



Thanks in advance.



</question>



<answer from>



a c
Member since: 05 November 2008
Total points: 106 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



At the grocery store they run about 4-6 US dollars for a 20 oz. bag (roughly 70 miniatures). I'm not sure how big of a bag you are talking about, but a quick search on ebay gave alot of results like 6(12oz) bags for $7 (240 pcs).



</answer>



<answer from>



kim t
Member since: 23 November 2007
Total points: 5086 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



In Alabama where I live, they had large bags of the mini peanutbutter cups for 4.98 at Walmart. They were the halloween version, but I'm sure you could get them all year round for about the same price.



</answer>

<question from>



JoJo
Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 160 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



How many ml make one oz?



How many milliliters makes one ounce



</question>



<answer from>



Obamas  Shoes
Member since: 15 October 2008
Total points: 1368 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



28



</answer>



<answer from>



hambone
Member since: 19 April 2006
Total points: 10839 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



it's actually 29.6 according to  this site. You are talking about fluid ounces, not weight ounces.



http://www.convert-me.com/en/convert/coo...



</answer>



<answer from>



msjantas...
Member since: 28 August 2008
Total points: 4087 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



Why?  I am not doing someones homework.



</answer>



<answer from>



Erica
Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 103 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Hambone has it right.  29.6mL make 1 ounce.  However, mL is a more precise way of measuring.  If your recipe calls for mL and you're changing to ounces, you might be adding too much or too little liquid, especially if you're baking (where every measurement has to be precise).



However, if you're changing from ounces to mL, you should be fine.



Source(s):



Baking is my passion.



</answer>

<answer>



Everyone has a different metabolism. I don't think anything is wrong with you, and heck, there's nothing wrong with eating food. It's better to eat than eating nothing at all! But there should be a good balance. Try the following:



When you eat, try chewing slowly. It's supposed to make you full - faster !



When you eat, try eating healthy food. Sometimes when we eat junk food, our body has that sense of 'well, let me keep eating more junk food! '. And you're actually introducing more fat.



If you want, try eating small portions of every meal. Remember we can eat 6 times a day! That's breakfast - snack - lunch - snack - dinner - snack. So, there's plenty to eat! In snacks, it's best to eat 100 calorie foods.



Always drink aprox. 8 glasses of water every day! Water actually makes you full every now and then. And - it's healthy. The more water, the better. Because you're actually cleaning your system.



</answer>

<answer>



"The fruit highest in Vitamin C, Guava, is native to Mexico, the Caribbean and Central America. 100 grams of Guava contains 228 mg of Vitamin C where one fruit contains about 128 mg....



Top 7 Fruits For Vitamin C Content
Guava, 1 medium, 165 mg
Papaya, 1 cup, 87 mg
Strawberries, 1 cup, 84 mg
Kiwi, 1 medium, 74 mg
Cantaloupe, 1 cup, 68 mg
Orange, 1 medium, 75 mg
Grapefruit, half, 42 mg."



Source(s):



http://www.formerfatguyblog.com/2008/03/...



</answer>



<answer from>



Michael G
Member since: 12 September 2007
Total points: 285 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Of all the natural sources of Vitamin C the kakadu plum and the camu camu fruit have the highest concentrations with about 3100mg and 2800mg per 100g respectively... Orange (commonly known as a source of Vitamin C) on the other hand only contains about 50mg per 100g... Strawberries are about 60mg and Blackcurrant is about 200mg!



Hope this helps you?



Source(s):



http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitamin_c#N...



</answer>

Heres a receipe for you:
BEER ROASTED CAT
1 cat cut into roast
1 can of Campbell's Cream of Mushroom soup
1 cube of beef bouillon
1 clove of garlic
1 Fine Irish Stout, a lot like a popular dark Irish Beer®, but NOT that brand at their lawyers' request. They alledge this article, educating others in the legal eating habits of over 100 million people world-wide, and specifically in rising East Asian markets, is "highly offensive."



Cover and soak cat roast in salt water for 24 hours. Drain water and then cover and soak in beer for 6 hours. Drain and place in crock pot with your cans of soup. Add a clove of garlic, and a cube of beef bouillon. If you start to slow cook your cat in the morning with your George Foreman Cooker (or it's ilk), you'll have finely cooked feline in time for supper.



If a slow cooker is not available, a cat can be baked at 350 degrees for 2-3 hours in a conventional oven and still come out pretty good. Beer Roasted Cat is fantastic served with mashed potatoes, collard greens, and fresh, homemade egg rolls. When planning a full meal just remember- cat is a course best served hot!



Cat may not be the most glamorous, or tastiest of game meats, but with a little thought and preparation, Baked Cat can make the belly of the persnicketiest diner glow with home baked goodness.

3rd Eye

<answer>



Your growing up.  We all have to learn and continue to learn how to control our emotions as we get older.



We all have "Pet Peeves" I guess you could say.  The only way to work through the emotions is to face them and ask at that time "what is it making me have this emotion".



More importantly, most emotions are determined by the environment you put yourself in.  Such as going to a club although you know it makes you feel uneasy, or watching a movie that makes you look at yourself in a bad way.



Its always great to have someone you can talk to about your emotions too, your not the only one that is going through what your going through.



In the future be more specific about the mood your questioning.  The answers get better.



Lastly are you out of shape, believe it or not most people go through mood swings when their bodies aren't happy,  Try eating healthier, especially veggies, you'd be surprise.



Have you ever seen a mad vegan.

<answer>



Here:



Description of ozone - American Heritage® Dictionary
NOUN: 1. An unstable, poisonous allotrope of oxygen, O3, that is formed naturally in the ozone layer from atmospheric oxygen by electric discharge or exposure to ultraviolet radiation, also produced in the lower atmosphere by the photochemical reaction of certain pollutants. It is a highly reactive oxidizing agent used to deodorize air, purify water, and treat industrial wastes. ozonic (-znk, -znk) , ozonous (zns)



Additional references: Columbia Encyclopedia, Wikipedia



</answer>

Is garlic a herb or a vegetable?

<answer>

</answer>



<answer from>



goodygoo...
Member since: 13 March 2008

</answer from>



<answer>



Both.  It's a root vegetable.



Herb, according to the all mighty wikipedia:
An herb is a plant grown for medicinal value or for flavoring food



It's used to flavor food and it has medicinal value.  But it's related to an onion, which is a root veggie.



So, yea, both.



</answer>

<question>



What is the difference in taste between Sauerkraut and Cole Slaw?



I have lived all 32 years of my life without trying Sauerkraut (I am kind of picky) and want to know if it tastes like cole slaw at all? I want to kind of get an idea of the taste before I try any ( I hate to waste food)..Thank you for answering and please excuse my culinary ignorance.



</question>



<answer from>



star08
Member since: 15 August 2008
Total points: 145 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Cole Slaw and Sauerkraut have very different taste. To start one is cold and the other is hot, both have cabbage as a common ingredient but taste totally different.
I personally like Sauerkraut



</answer>



<answer from>



Dindi
Member since: 25 July 2008
Total points: 1569 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Cole slaw has a base of cabbage and carrots with vinegar and mostly mayonnaise taste and has a sweetness to it.  Sauerkraut has the base of cabbage and has been in a vinegar brine, like pickles and is very sower.  If you love dill pickles, you will like sauerkraut, although sauerkraut is stronger in taste than dill pickles.  Cole slaw is served cold.  Sauerkraut should be served warm.



</answer>

NASOOSHi...

<answer>



im not going to copy and paste a long wikipedia section on this.



basically, a fruit has seeds while a vegetable does not. it doesn't matter if it is sweet.



surprisingly, cucumbers/avocados are fruits.



</answer>



<answer from>



tolerant...
Member since: 24 October 2008
Total points: 591 (Level 2)

<answer>



He he nice try!  sweet B



Acutally fruit bears its own seed, within itself (apples) or on its surface (strawberries).  Vegetable seeds come from flowers which grow on the mature plants as they 'go to seed'.



Tomato is a fruit.

<answer from>

<answer>



Nutella ™ Cheesecake



2 (8 ounce) packages cream cheese, softened



1/2 cup white sugar



1 (13 ounce) jar chocolate hazelnut spread (nutella)



1/4 teaspoon vanilla extract



1 (9 inch) prepared graham cracker crust



In a large bowl, beat cream cheese and sugar until smooth. Blend in Nutella and vanilla until no streaks remain. pour into crust. Refrigerate for at least 4 hours before serving.



</answer>

<answer>



You know those lovely French pains au chocolat that look like a chocolate sausage roll? My favourite way of eating nutella is to recreate them by cutting a slit in the top of a croissant and inserting a spoonfull or two inside, then microwave for 10 seconds. That's breakfast.



Then pancakes - About a half pint milk, 4 tablespoons flour and a couple of eggs, fling together in jug. Beat. I'm a bit vague on quantities so add more flour if mix looks too thin. A couple of spoonfulls fried in hot olive oil, flip, cooked pancake onto plate, filled with nutella and rolled, Greek yoghurt, sliced banana and golden granulated sugar on the top. Or skip the yoghurt and banana. That's lunch.



Something green and healthy for dinner. Then half melted icecream and nutella folded through for pudding.

<question>



Can any one explain how to prepare green tea?



</question>



<answer from>



Kimmi
Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 102 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



seriously? you put it in a cup with water and then put it in the microwave.



</answer>



<answer from>



trees750...
Member since: 17 July 2008
Total points: 7600 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



Heat your water to just off the boiling point.  Use good water.  If your tap water tastes bad, use a bottled water you like.  Green tea has a delicate flavor and bad water will affect it's taste.



Pour hot water into a cup or teapot.  Add your tea.  Steep (usually) for 3 - 5 minutes.  Longer for stonger tea, shorter for weaker tea.  Drink and enjoy.



The below link has a lot of information on brewing tea, if you want to really get into it.



Source(s):



http://www.o-cha.com/brew.htm



</answer>

<question>



Why do we boil milk two three times a day?



</question>



<answer from>



sunny112...
Member since: 27 June 2007
Total points: 1431 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Milk sold in supermarkets is pasteurised and does not need boiling.  You only need to boil raw milk (from your own cows/goats/sheep or a farm you trust).  Too much heating destroys vitamins so if you want a warm milk drink just warm it, don't boil it.



</answer>



<answer from>



b_wells_...
Member since: 04 September 2008
Total points: 369 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



I you live in a country that pasteurizes milk then you are wasting your time it is unnecessary (as long as it remains cool aka. fridge). Boiling it kills off bacteria and keeps it from spoiling but if it is pasteurized then it normally can be drunk before building up any noticeable amounts of bacteria.



</answer>

What are some foods that have a lot of SALT in them?



I need to eat salty snacks...??

Member since: 27 April 2008

<answer>



Campbell's Soup, definitely.



Bake goods including cakes, cookies, pies, pastries, sweet rolls, doughnuts, pancakes, waffles, biscuits and muffins.



Grains including rice or noodles with seasoning packets and sauces, such as Ramen noodles, rice pilaf, instant potatoes and stuffing mix.



Potatoes including au gratin, scalloped, packaged with sauces and seasoning mixes.



Sauces including soy sauce, teriyaki sauce, Worcestershire sauce, steak sauce, barbecue sauce, smoke-flavored sauces, gravies, marinades, pasta sauces like marinara and alfredo, chili sauce, cocktail sauce, tomato puree and tomato sauce.



Condiments and dressings including pickle relish, catsup, mayonnaise, commercial and packaged salad dressings.



Commercially prepared main entrees including most frozen dinners or frozen main entrees, pot pies, canned main entrees such as hash, stew, chili, entrees with seasoning mixes such as macaroni and cheese.



Most Asian foods including Chinese and Japanese foods made with teriyaki or soy sauce; and East Indian, Thai and Vietnamese unless prepared without added sauces containing salt or sodium products.



Most Mexican foods including tacos, enchiladas, burritos and tamales.



Pizza, lasagna, manicotti, ravioli, quiche, soufflés, blintzes and cheese rarebit.



http://www.pamf.org/heartfailure/lifesty...



</answer>



<answer from>



gnightgr...
Member since: 02 November 2008
Total points: 248 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Other than potato chips and peanuts, here is a list of High Sodium Foods:
A cup of canned soup has 1,000 mg of sodium, a cup of chili has 1,200 mg, a typical TV dinner has 1,150 mg and a slice of pizza has 900 mg. One hot dog has 900 mg of sodium, 1 oz of parmesan cheese has 500 mg of sodium and 3 oz of ham has 1,100 mg. Other high-salt items you might take by mouth include alkalizers, cough medicines, laxatives, mineral waters and pain relievers.



Source(s):



http://www.meniett.com/dietary_treatment...



</answer>

<question from>



dghk.sjb...
Member since: 18 January 2008
Total points: 313 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



How do beans grow?  ?



</question>



<answer from>



sunny112...
Member since: 27 June 2007
Total points: 1433 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Beans grow in pods, like peas (lots of them side by side in a long sheath).  Some beans are harvested green (immature), such as French or runner beans.  Most other beans are left to mature on the vine, dried then hulled (dry sheath removed).  If you want to plant beans, put some dry beans in the ground in spring, about 10cm apart.  Once seedlings appear they will need a support to climb up.



</answer>



<answer from>



trees750...
Member since: 17 July 2008
Total points: 7600 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



They grow above ground on vines.  If you want to see one grow, get a couple of dried pinto beans.  Put them between several damp paper towels, of wrap the towels around a clear jar.  Put the beans between the towels and the glass so you can see them.



Keep the towels damp. Put in a window, but not in direct sun.  The beans will sprout in a few days.  You'll even get a little bean plant if you keep the towels wet.



Source(s):



Gardening since I was a kid and relatives that are farmers.



</answer>

Member since: 04 November 2008
Total points: 105 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



apple juice mixed in equal parts; with clean / filtered water is best.
look for juice with no preservatives & no added sugar.



*its what the ambos here recommend for ppl who have heat stroke / dehydration  etc.



most sodas (even lemonades) contain caffeine, so avoid them.



to begin with, make the decision to stop buying it. you may find the going difficult for a few days, but it is easier to resist the product at the store, than when its sitting in your house!



as a former smoker i know that i cannot have just one cigarette.
out of necessity i assumed the viewpoint of extremes (with nothing in between) of either smoking a pack a day, or not smoking at all, because of the escalating nature of addiction, in which; the more the substance is consumed, the more it is craved & so on..



it is important to keep this in mind once we are clear of our addictions, because dangerous thinking can lead to a pitfall.



the confidence that recovery builds can give us a false sense that we have conquered our addictions in such a way that we can toy with them.
can you just drink one? if you cannot control it, its better not to have it. ever.



if you must have caffiene, try making a refreshing iced tea with lemon & honey, to gently wean off it.
..or try 1 Tblsp apple cider vinegar with honey mixed in water; it is a very healthful drink-it will give you more of a buzz than any soda pop!



you may also benefit from buying a urinary alkaliser such as citravescent, which contains baking soda, (available from chemists) to regulate the acidity caused by excessive amounts of sugar (which can rob calcium from your bones). these drinks contain electrolytes, like gatorade (but minus the testicle-shrinking brominated oils lol)



but the apple cider vinegar will help reduce acidity also.



even if you cant kick your habit, you can minimize damage by steering clear of artificial diet flavours, as the chemicals can be very harmful.



also, take a look at how your addiction developed. do you watch a lot of tv? when we watch tv we open ourselves to being programmed by the will of advertisers.



dont forget the most important aspect of life is to look after your soul, which never dies.



make sure you have a good relationship with the Lord :D
ask  Him for help. it was He who helped me quit smoking.
Glory to God!



Source(s):



spiritlessons.com



</answer>

<question>



What exactly are saltines?

Thanks :)

<answer from>

</answer from>



<answer>



Small  biscuits,salty. eaten with alcoholic drinks.cookery book



Source(s):



cookery books



</answer>



<answer from>



Skippy Newbaum
Member since: 27 October 2008
Total points: 380 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



A saltine or soda cracker is a thin, usually square cracker made from white flour, shortening, yeast, and baking soda, with some varieties lightly sprinkled with coarse salt. It has perforations throughout its surface, to allow steam to escape for uniform rising, and along the edges, as individual crackers are broken from larger sheets during manufacture. It has a very dry and crisp texture, as it is made with less shortening than varieties such as Ritz crackers.



Some familiar brand names of saltine crackers in the United States are Nabisco's Premium and Keebler's Zesta. Low-sodium saltines as well as unsalted-top versions are commonly available. Also available in stores are whole-wheat saltines.



Source(s):



http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saltine_cra...



</answer>

<answer from>



Diane B
Member since: 25 January 2007
Total points: 20989 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



A chef is a person who cooks professionally. In a professional kitchen setting, the term is used only for the one person in charge of everyone else in the kitchen, the executive chef.



A cook follows the instructions set forth by the chef.  In the case of a diner or a place like Denny's, there is no chef, all are cooks usually called "short order cooks"



</answer>



<answer from>



leigh h
Member since: 17 September 2008
Total points: 1263 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



I guess it varies from place to place, but in all the places I've worked a chef is a person who has chosen to make a career of cooking and is passionate about food.
For them, being a chef is a profession and not just a job.



A cook is someone who comes into work and does whatever they're told for the paycheque at the end.



For them, being a cook is a job and not a profession.



</answer>

<question>



Why are there different color twist ties on the bread in the grocery store?



I noticed blue ties, green ties, red ties, white ties...I don't get it?



</question>



<answer from>



yesisaid...
Member since: 08 April 2008
Total points: 115 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Bread is delivered on regular basis. Each day has a different color twist tie. They are:



Monday- Blue
Tuesday- Green
Thursday- Red
Friday- White
Saturday- Yellow



So today being Tuesday, I want a green tie - not red which is Thursday (almost na week old?)



Source(s):



Collrctrd on the internet 2001. www.snopes.com/foodprepare/breading.htm



I had this for a few years, so check it out.



</answer>

<question>



How should i store bell peppers? ?



I just bought some bell pepers at the local farmers market and wanted them to last abot a week or so whats the best way to keep them. Thank you



</question>



<answer from>



kiwi
Member since: 27 November 2006
Total points: 6363 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



They last best in the fridge.



</answer>



<answer from>



blah blah
Member since: 24 October 2007
Total points: 157 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



fridge



Source(s):



blah blah



</answer>



<answer from>



calder28
Member since: 05 November 2007
Total points: 198 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



They should be fine for a week in a closed bag or container in the fridge.



</answer>



<answer from>



jessic4
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 107 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Place whole, unwashed peppers in a sealed plastic bag and refrigerate for a week or more. Beware of any excess moisture in the bag that could cause peppers to spoil. Red, orange, and yellow peppers are fully ripe and need to be eaten sooner. Peppers store best at 50°F.



Source(s):



http://www.angelicorganics.com/Vegetable...



</answer>

<question from>



kiya12bc
Member since: 18 February 2007
Total points: 6777 (Level 5)



</question from>



<question>



China & the melamine problem.?



With all the stuff coming out of China, food in particular is what I am asking about.  Do the labels for food sold in the U. S. show SOMEWHERE, on that label whether the food is produced/made/ingredients from China?  The milk was bad enough, but now there is candy out there etc.,  can any of you inform the rest of us how to check and look out for this?



</question>



<answer from>



Soda
Member since: 11 May 2008
Total points: 10667 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Well, starting today, the USDA is making it so that retailers have to put stickers on foods (meats, veggies and fruits) showing where they originated from. Some retailers will have that on packaged products but I guess we will have to see how that works. I couldn't tell one how to look for melamine tainted products because those recalled items were simply contaminated. Melamine would never make it on an ingredients label. This has been going on for about a decade with recalled items leading back to China. The only thing I could suggest is to look at the labeling and if it's manufactured, processed or originating from China, find an alternative.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Thanks. I knew they wouldn't list melamine on the label, but just hadn't/haven't paid attention as to country of origin or country for ingredients.. and didn't know if that was/would be listed..Thanks again!



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



lemonlim...
Member since: 15 February 2006
Total points: 5551 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



The answer is yes and no. We may not know where all the ingredients come from. But if the food or for instance toothpaste is processed somewhere so the country of Origin is listed on the packaging. Food since it is processed on such a large scale these days is a crap shoot anyway. Let see lettuce, sprouts, apples, apple juice, hamburger, jalapeno pepers and even fresh tomatos. Buy more locally from smaller American producers and go the the farmer's market.



</answer>

<answer from>



rgentry2...
Member since: 26 November 2007
Total points: 1514 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Geez, I don't know why people get on here and just throw out blind guesses at answers.  This is a good question with a lot of stupid answers given.  Here are the facts.



Chewing gum can make you lose weight, not because of the negligible amount of calories it burns though.  Your body sort of has a mind of its own if you will.  Hunger is a very complex reflex, and you can trick your body into thinking you are not hungry anymore by doing certain things.  One of those things is chewing.  In fact, when you sit down to a normal meal, if you chew your food more, you will find that you will eat less.  So, chewing gum can actually trick part of the body's hunger reflex into thinking you are not hungry, so as a result you will eat less and lose weight.



However, like I said, hunger is very complex, so there are many more factors that come into play such as smells, calorie intake, sugar intake, physical exertion, etc.



</answer>



<answer from>



Drummer for life!
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 107 (Level 1)

<answer from>



Atheist
Member since: 20 January 2008
Total points: 6127 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



You need to read up on what Veal really is.



It's not the fact that it's a young cow.



Veal calves are immobilized for the entire period of their life. They are often kept in very small boxes to prevent them from ever sitting down, turning around or moving. They are typically kept in the dark and fed with a feeding tube so their neck muscles don't start to toughen up.



If they're not in a box, they're chained to the floor where they cannot stand, look around or move.



Lambs, however, are allowed to frolic free in a field with their herd. They're not restrained and confined. They're not tortured just to keep their young meat tender.



</answer>



<answer from>



Jack
Member since: 23 January 2007
Total points: 168 (Level 1)

<question>



Are Diet Coke & Coke Zero the same?



Are they the same with different name or are they different with their ingredients and taste???



</question>



<answer from>



Jester Dan
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 107 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



No. diet coke has less calories and coke zero has no sugar



</answer>



<answer from>



Guite
Member since: 01 October 2008
Total points: 105 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Coke Zero is sweetened with a combination of aspartame and acesulfame potassium (Ace-K). Coke Zero is the same basic formula as classic Coke while Diet Coke is a different formula completely. Diet Coke is sweetened with aspartame only. There are unsubstantiated theories (at least by Coca Cola) that the unsuccessful release of Coke Two or new Coke was actually the formula for Diet Coke, just sweetened with the classic sugar combination.



Also, Coke Zero has 0.5 kilocalories per 100ml while Diet Coke, oddly enough, still contains one calorie.



One other rational for the Coca Cola release of Coke Zero is that men are reluctant to buy diet coke because of the association with dieting and women. Much of the marketing of Coke Zero in the US is directed toward men and activities often associated with masculinity.



On a side note, in many european countries and pan american/south american countries, Coke Zero is released as Coca Cola Light.



Source(s):



http://wiki.answers.com/Q/What_is_the_di...



</answer>



<answer from>



S0 NUMB
Member since: 15 November 2007
Total points: 1341 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Yes, they just package it differently to sell more product...



</answer>

<question from>



nallama8...

</question from>



<question>



How are baked beans made?



I know this sounds like a silly question but what beans are used to make baked beans and how do they make it.



Thanks



</question>



<answer from>



mitty_2k...
Member since: 30 September 2008
Total points: 158 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Heinz use haricot beans



Source(s):



Most commercial canned baked beans such as Heinz are made from haricot beans, also known as Boston Beans or Navy Beans, a variety of Phaseolus vulgaris, and sold in a sauce. In the United Kingdom, tomato sauce is most commonly used.



</answer>



<answer from>



cin2win
Member since: 11 October 2007
Total points: 23202 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Cooking & Recipes



</answer from>



<answer>



1 pound dried navy white beans, soaked overnight and drained



recipe



1 pound bacon, diced



2 cups diced onions



1 tablespoon chopped garlic



1 pound dried navy white beans, soaked overnight and drained



1/2 cup Steen's 100 percent Pure Cane Syrup



1/2 cup light brown sugar



2 1/2 cups ketchup



1/4 cup yellow mustard



Salt and black pepper



1 gallon chicken stock



2 bay leaves



Directions
In a large pot, over medium heat, add the bacon and render until crispy, about 4 to 6 minutes. Add the onions and continue to saute for 3 to 4 minutes. Season with salt and pepper. Stir in the garlic and beans and cook for 1 minute. Stir in the cane syrup, brown sugar, ketchup and mustard. Season with salt and pepper. Mix thoroughly. Stir in the chicken stock. Bring the liquid to a boil and reduce to a simmer. Cook the beans for about 4 hours, or until tender, stirring occasionally. From time to time, one might need to add a little water at a time if the beans need some to prevent burning.



</answer>



<answer from>



accurist...
Member since: 13 June 2008
Total points: 3023 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



You get a bean and you bake it, and voila! Baked bean!



Source(s):



For "baked beans" use more than one.



</answer>

<question>



Safe to thaw my steak in the fridge?



Is it safe to thaw my steak in my fridge before i eat it tonight? The package has already been opened since i eat half the meat earlier this week. Is it safe to thaw a half-opened package of steak in the fridge then eat it tonite?



</question>



<answer from>



Shawna
Member since: 25 April 2007
Total points: 185 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



you should be fine.  I would suggest putting it on a plate before putting it in your fridge.  once it starts to thaw it can be a mess.  depending also on how big it is, you may get a better result eating it tomorrow night.  Sometimes meat can take two days to defrost completely



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Gonna do exactly this, checked the steak, and its much too frozen for tonight... so im gonna cook it tomorrow nite! wish me luck!
Thanks for everyones quick feedback!



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



Curious
Member since: 06 May 2008
Total points: 5624 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



So let me get this straight - you opened a package of steak, cooked half immediately and then froze the other half, uncooked - right? In that case, yes you can thaw the steak in your fridge, assuming that you bought it fresh and it was never frozen, or you bought it frozen and it never thawed the first time.



What you should NOT do is freeze the meat, thaw it, and then refreeze it without cooking it.



However, if you thaw it, cook it, and then freeze it again, it's ok.



That said, depending on the size of the steak, one day in the fridge might not be long enough to thaw it - but give it a try! You can also defrost it in the microwave, or in a plastic bag (like a Ziploc) in hot water.



</answer>



<answer from>



Heavenl...
Member since: 21 April 2008
Total points: 163 (Level 1)

<question from>



Kristine Kochanski
Member since: 28 June 2008
Total points: 1742 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



Have you ever made your own Sloe Gin?



</question>



<answer from>



MiMi
Member since: 27 June 2008
Total points: 2610 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



No.  But it might be fun to learn how.



</answer>



<answer from>



mad
Member since: 20 June 2006
Total points: 13971 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



Yes - it was very nice too! Here's a recipe:
Ingredients
450g/1lb sloes
225g/8oz caster sugar
1 litre/1¾ pint gin



Method
1. Prick the tough skin of the sloes all over with a clean needle and put in a large sterilised jar.
2. Pour in the sugar and the gin, seal tightly and shake well.
3. Store in a cool, dark cupboard and shake every other day for a week. Then shake once a week for two months.
4. The sloe gin will now be a beautiful dark red and ready to drink, although it will still improve with keeping.
5. Variation: make blackberry brandy in the same way, substituting blackberries for the sloes and brandy for the gin. Blackberries do not need pricking.



Source(s):



BBC recipes



</answer>

</answer>



<answer from>



annie
Member since: 18 July 2008
Total points: 660 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



If you have been a vegetarian that long than starting with chicken is a good idea. Just take it slow. You don't want to start out eating any meats that are really greasy



</answer>



<answer from>



kayamat_...
Member since: 21 November 2006
Total points: 726 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Just think ALSO about the following:-



Patrick Wall, chairman of the European Food Safety Authority, recently asked whether it is "morally or ethically correct" to feed grain to animals while people starve. Rearing animals for human consumption is a shocking waste of resources: 16lbs of grain are needed to produce just 1lb of animal flesh. The world's cattle alone consume the same amount of calories it would take to feed more 8.7 billion people – that’s more than the entire human population on Earth.



Some more statistics for you: ninety per cent of the agricultural land in the UK is used to raise livestock, but still we do not have enough grain and so we import 46 million tonnes annually from developing countries. These are countries which not only suffer environmental degradation as a result but, in many cases, cannot afford to feed their own people. Every day, 24,000 people die from hunger and hunger-related causes; 75 per cent of them children less than five years old. Meanwhile, millions of tonnes of grain are being siphoned off to feed animals destined for the already groaning dining tables of countries with the fattest populations in the world.



Factory farming puts a serious strain on our water supplies too. While millions face drought, much of the world's water supply is diverted to animal agriculture. A study this year by the Stockholm International Water Institute, the Food and Agriculture Organisation and the International Water Management Institute found it takes up to 4,000 litres of water to produce one kilogramme of wheat but up to 20,000 litres of water to produce one kilogramme of beef. A totally vegetarian diet requires 300 gallons of water per day, while a meat-eating diet requires more than 4,000 gallons of water per day.



Source(s):



http://style.uk.msn.com/wellbeing/health...



</answer>

<answer>

From a purely medical point of view then introduce it slowly and make sure it has been WELL cooked.



</answer>

<question from>

</question from>



<question>



Best way to carve a roast chicken to get most meat off and it doesnt go all shreddy?



</question>



<additional details>



i hate shreddy chicken i like chunks of meat =)



</additional details>



<answer from>



buildypu...
Member since: 23 August 2006
Total points: 2003 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Use an Electric knife



</answer>



<answer from>



enfin28
Member since: 17 June 2007
Total points: 181 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Never carve meat straight from the oven..allow to rest for a while for the juices to settle before carving. Then pull the skin back from the breast and it should be easier.



</answer>



<answer from>



Kaz
Member since: 18 November 2007
Total points: 1128 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Leave to stand for 20-30mins and make sure you have a very sharp knife.



</answer>



<answer from>



Becky Boo
Member since: 21 September 2006
Total points: 195 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Forget that. LET it go all shreddy, that's the best way to eat chicken.

Just like mum used to make.  (she can't carve!)



</answer>



<answer from>



RussetB
Member since: 12 June 2007
Total points: 1934 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Use a sharp knife and let the knife do most of the work - don't force it.



</answer>



<answer from>



Red Death
Member since: 19 March 2008
Total points: 1171 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Let it sit at least 20 minutes lightly covered to let the juices reabsorb into the meat.  Cut the skin between the leg/thigh and body and break the thigh from the body.  Cut this off and separate thigh and leg if desired.
cut and pull wing away from the body as much as you can (doesn't have to be totally removed yet) Start slicing the breast with a cut just above wing running all the way down the the "fanny" end.  Then cut the top of the breast downward toward the first cut moving the knife along the ribs to get the most of the breast in one slice (this takes practice).  Repeat other side.  After you have 2 "slabs" of breast meat, you can put it on a cutting board and slice it into serving size pieces (or if you're like my husband, he'll take the whole thing!!)



Good luck.



</answer>



<answer from>



fed up woman
Member since: 15 April 2006
Total points: 13919 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



Rest for at least 20 minutes and carve as parallel to the backbone as possible.



</answer>

<answer from>



Karen B
Member since: 16 August 2008
Total points: 155 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



White Chocolate Cake



Submitted by: VanDerStad
Rated: 4 out of 5 by 68 members 	Prep Time: 20 Minutes
Cook Time: 35 Minutes 	Ready In: 55 Minutes
Yields: 12 servings
"This is a very heavy white chocolate cake with a white chocolate frosting. It is a family favorite that is requested at every family gathering."
INGREDIENTS:
2 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
1 teaspoon baking soda
1/2 teaspoon baking powder
1/2 teaspoon salt
6 (1 ounce) squares white
chocolate, chopped
1/2 cup hot water
1 cup butter, softened
1 1/2 cups white sugar
3 eggs



1 cup buttermilk



6 (1 ounce) squares white
chocolate, chopped
2 1/2 tablespoons all-purpose
flour
1 cup milk
1 cup butter, softened
1 cup white sugar
1 teaspoon vanilla extract
DIRECTIONS:
1. 	Preheat oven to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C). Sift together the 2 1/2 cups flour, baking soda, baking powder and salt. Set aside.
2. 	In small saucepan, melt 6 ounces white chocolate and hot water over low heat. Stir until smooth, and allow to cool to room temperature.
3. 	In a large bowl, cream 1 cup butter and 1 1/2 cup sugar until light and fluffy. Add eggs one at a time, beating well with each addition. Stir in flour mixture alternately with buttermilk. Mix in melted white chocolate and 1 1/2 teaspoon vanilla.
4. 	Pour batter into two 9 inch round cake pans. Bake for 30 to 35 minutes in the preheated oven, until a toothpick inserted into the center of the cake comes out clean.
5. 	To make Frosting: In a medium bowl, combine 6 ounces white chocolate, 2 1/2 tablespoons flour and 1 cup milk. Cook over medium heat, stirring constantly, until mixture is very thick. Cool completely.
6. 	In large bowl, cream 1 cup butter, 1 cup sugar and 1 teaspoon vanilla; beat until light and fluffy. Gradually add cooled white chocolate mixture. Beat at high speed until it is the consistency of whipped cream. Spread between layers, on top and sides of cake.
ALL RIGHTS RESERVED © 2008 Allrecipes.com



Source(s):



http://allrecipes.com/Recipe-Tools/Print...



</answer>

<answer from>



geetanjali k
Member since: 28 May 2008
Total points: 355 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Green Tea is a SUPERFOOD!! It tastes great and has many health benefits --
*It is traditionally used to alleviate stomach problems, vomiting, and diarrhea. 
*It's also been found to reduce blood pressure, cholesterol levels, and blockages of the blood vessels in the heart that can lead to heart attacks. 
*Herbalists claim Green Tea also has powerful anti-cancer properties and believe that it is also useful in treating some bacterial infections.
*The May 2008 issue of the American Thoracic Society's American Journal of Respiratory and Critical Care Medicine reported that green tea polyphenols (GTP, for short) actually helped in reducing the memory loss and inflammation that afflict sleep apnea sufferers.
*Studies in Japan have shown that people who drink five or more cups of green tea each day are sixteen per cent less likely to suffer from coronary artery disease.
*Green Tea may also be good for people who want to lose weight. It is a natural diuretic.
*It also has cosmetic benefits – Green Tea extracts help the skin to reduce wrinkling, leathering and premature skin aging.



As for drinking it in a citurs flavour, I think it should be fine. In fact scientists have discovered that mixing green tea with other substances, such as citrus juices, vitamin C and even soy milk and rice milk, increases the amount of the antioxidants that can be absorbed by the body!

Happy drinking!!



Source(s):



http://copperwiki.org/index.php/Green_te...



</answer>

<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



I am a former chef and the people who have suggested Digestives or Mc Vities Biscuit are correct any wholemeal biscuit or sweet tea biscuit, processed in a food mill or MagiMix to crumbs is fine and if it is for cheesecake or a pastry base, just melt some butter or marg and a bit of dark brown sugar, and mix it like sage and onion stuffing to a meal and press it into the cake tin for baking.

I made an American style cheesecake for my friends in Liverpool and now that all they make for guest at tea or over for dinner.

<answer>



Ritz crackers are not the same as graham crackers.

Graham crackers are a bit sweet.  They are light brown in color.  You may call them biscuits in the UK.  Another way I think of them as is a healthy non frosted cookie.  In the US we eat them plain or often crush them and use them with a little melted butter and sugar to press into a pie tin for a crust.  Cheesecakes often have this crust.



</answer>

<question>



Whats the difference ???



whats the difference between yellow, green and red curry paste?? 
is it a different flavour, hotness, ingredients, ethnicity ????



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Green Curry Paste - uses fresh herbs and spices 
Red Curry Paste - uses dried herbs and spices 
Yellow Curry Paste - contains cinnamon but no coriander roots



</answer>

<answer from>



chef robert
Member since: 04 June 2006
Total points: 461 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



cooking comes form the heart.

So if you have the desire and passion to please someone by cooking for them or just for you. you can do it.

A few tips
1, get a good resource for the recipes you are looking for. The internet has some cook resources. BE careful, some internet recipes don't work. a library will be a good resourec for good cook books.
2. tools and equipment
Make sure you have the right tools and equipment.
Example; if the recipe calls for a cast iron pan, get a cast iron pan.
Sharp knives also help the preparation
3. Ingredients. 
Fresh, fresh , fresh and preprae your food so it is ready when you are ready to eat.
4. read the recipe 2 times. make your grocery list. 
read the recipe before you start cooking.
5 Then follow the recipe.



Chef robert author of Chef Robert Presents Romantic Dinners for Two
www.romanticdinnersfortwo.com



</answer>

<answer from>



lil'ros...
Member since: 30 September 2007
Total points: 219 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Everything a host and a hostess do is the same. A host is a male while the hostess is a female. They both invite, welcome, and entertain guests, often providing them with food and drink.



</answer>



<answer from>



Nom De Plume
Member since: 20 June 2008
Total points: 846 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Host can be a general term for someone who's hosting a party, a program, or the likes. It's someone who entertains guests either at home or elsewhere.

Synonyms:
entertainer, toastmaster, master, mistress, hostess, talk-show moderator, master of ceremonies, mistress of ceremonies, M.C., emcee

Hostess: same definition, but specifically used for a female host.



Source(s):



yourdictionary.com



</answer>

As we appear to be on the brink of a global food crisis, is it time to rethink farming methods? How?



Given that we appear to be on the brink of a global food crisis, should we be making the world's farms even bigger and more efficient, or should we be making them smaller? Is it time to dismantle the industrial food machine, or should we be cranking it up to the next level?

<answer>



I believe that in considering the global food shortage governments/corporations are looking at the wrong side of the equation.
On the same side of this equation is a shortage of fuel, most commodities and even water. Add the pressure on public services and infrastructure and one sees that the problem is the other side of the equation - too many people. Rather than control population, governments and greedy corporations requiring more retail sales have heavily subsidised the production of people in the lower socio-economic groups.
In the West, this has been the cause of housing shortage, over crowded roads, poor public services, over working of many who are employed and the creation of a consuming but non-contributing underclass. Population control will solve world commodity shortages and improve the quality of life for the majority of people.

Specifically on farming, I favour minimum dependence on imports, to be effected by subsidy at the point of production rather than guaranteed sale price which can create unwanted surpluses. Subject to these controls, let the market determine the most effective production methods. 
On GM crops: why risk letting the corporation that inspired 'Silent Spring' become the architect of 'Mutant Millennium'?
GM has its place - in the laboratory. We should try to move away from high dependence on agri-chemicals, possibly balancing lower yields with the reduced production costs.



</answer>

</answer from>



<answer>



Farming methods have nothing to do with the level of hunger in the world. We already create more than enough food for every single person on this mudball to stuff themselves until they drop dead from overeating. The U.N.'s Population Reference Bureau is quite clear that the main cause of hunger in the world today is poverty. In their landmark study on hunger, “Population, Food, and Nutrition” they don’t even consider increased food production as a possible solution to the hunger problem. Hunger still exists because many poor people around the world lack the resources to buy enough food. In other words, people are starving to death (more correctly, being starved to death) through poverty, not though lack of food. It's pointless trying to work out why poverty exists in the world,  but considering the money thrown at the problem – the G8 summit increased aid to Africa from $25 billion to $50 billion US in 2005 – it is certainly an intractable one. What desperate sinkhole of poverty couldn’t be cured by fifty billion dollars?

The fact remains that we produce enough food to supply all six billion people on this planet with a massive excess left over. There is so much food available, in fact, that everyone who can afford it has a plentiful supply. This is what the United Nations has to say on the subject:

“... Despite the dire predictions that the world’s population would soon outstrip food production, it has been the other way around: food production has risen a full 16 per cent above population growth. The American Association for the Advancement of Science has noted that 78 per cent of the world’s malnourished children live in countries with food surpluses. Clearly, this condition indicates a need for a keener social conscience and better political leadership ....There is enough food to go around now and for at least the next half-century. The world is not going to run out of food for all.”  (http://www.goveg.com/worldhunger)

It is not a matter of making more food. We don’t need to. We already make more than enough. The problem is with food distribution. Food surpluses in Europe and the United States are either suppressed by subsidies to farmers who agree not to grow certain crops during periods of overproduction, or they are destroyed. They are not loaded into bulk grain carriers and shipped to areas of the world blighted by famine. If they were the problem might be solved. Might.



How can we have a net surplus of food in the world while a significant proportion of the human population is not merely undernourished but starving to death en masse? Given that it is true that "Due to advances in agriculture of many countries, there is now a substantial world surplus of food"  (Abelson, P.H. (1972). World Food. Science, 236,9.)  how is it that “more people than ever before are undernourished or malnourished”. (Curtain, M.E. (1985 July). Development and food. Inter-American Development Bank News, p. 3.)

The standard economic definition of surplus is not just ‘too much’, as you would think it might be. Economists can make anything more complex than it needs to be, that’s why they have a Nobel Prize just for them. “Surplus” is defined as a supply situation where buyers do not exhaust available supply while still paying a unit price acceptable to sellers. Right. Glad we got that sorted out. Used in connection with world population and their food requirements, the words "food surplus" are worse than misleading. Only from food producers' point of view is there surplus. From many potential customers, there is shortage. There is widespread famine even in countries that are net exporters of food. (Poleman, T.T. (1969). World food: A perspective. Science, 173, 510-518) There is surplus largely because millions of people in these countries simply don’t have the financial clout to create an economic demand sufficient to interest suppliers. (Wortman, S. (1980). World food and nutrition: The scientific and technological base. Science, 209, 157- 164.)



For example in India the National Institute of Nutrition estimated that as many as 50% of rural households and 55% of urban slum households do not have enough food to meet daily energy requirements. Yet India exports massive amounts of food and makes huge export income as a result. The food has been distributed out of the country and away from starving people because they cannot afford to buy it, and consumers in other countries can. India exports rice, wheat, sugarcane, tea, cotton, jute, cashews, coffee, spices, “other vegetables”, melons, sorghum, millet, corn, barley, chickpeas, bananas, and mangoes, all of which are desperately needed by their indigent, underfed people, none of whom can afford to pay the prices we Westerners can.

We make enough food for the entire population of the world. Food shortages are caused by poverty and inequitable distribution of food, not the lack of food supplies.



</answer>



<answer from>



no answerer details



</answer from>

<answer>



I think we need to get back to smaller scale farming, run self sufficiently. That is, you rear your livestock free range, you use their waste on the land, and the produce of the land to feed both you and them.

That is the ideal for me anyway. The problem is getting there and making it succesful enough to feed an entire population. The biggest problem will be to wean farms off chemicals. Chemicals cause all kinds of problems with the soil, problems that are alliviated with yet more chemicals until, with out the chemicals, the land is useless. All this land would need to have lots of natural fertiliser and manure put into first, but whilst that is happening where do you crow your crops. You could do half your land at a time I suppose but the shortfall in produce would have to be made up by imports, leading to all sorts of financial headaches for the farmers, which would either have to be propped up by susidies or simple left to go bust under pressure from foreign competition.

Self sufficient, natural, clean farming is a wonderful idea, but there are simple too many mouths to feed in the world and too many desperate countries willing to fill them with cheap and nasty produce.

Personally I grow my own, not enough to be entirely self sufficient, but enough to not have to rely too much on Tesco's. I think if we all did this it might put enough pressure on supermarkets and farmers to produce affordable (let's face it, it not cheap) organic fruit and veg at least, if not ethical meat.

PS: I really liked your elderflower champagne recipe. Unfortunately it exploded all over my shed:) Still, what was left was quite nice.



Source(s):



Just common sense from growing my own. 
www.pdblake.com



</answer>

<answer>



In countries like the UK, so much is wasted.  I don't really think we have a problem, especially if people would stop throwing out perfectly good food.  By making the farms here even bigger we'll just all end up eating bendy luminous carrots with no flavour, and put many more already struggling farmers out of business.

Globally, farming methods need to be improved.  For example using simple fertilisers on the soil to increase productivity, introducing more cooperative farming groups and diversifying the food that is grown might help to alleviate the threat of famine in developing countries.  Additionally I think that inter-country trade could be improved to help small scale farmers who might want to grow some cash crops, and also to diversify what is available in the market place for people to buy.



The market place in developing countries just isn't good enough at the moment, and those who can and/or want to sell extra food often don't have access to the demand for this food.  Currently, so many small scale farmers who have the potential to increase their production have no motivation to do so, as they don't have access to the market place where their excess produce is really needed, and so they stick to subsitance farming.

<answer>



I think that agriculture, at least in developed nations, is changing for the better. Probably at the pace that will be least jarring to the markets.
Agriculture in some developing nations, due to the good work of NGO's, individuals and education, is also changing for the better. But far too slowly.
That said, in an ideal world, I would advocate the total overhaul of food production and distribution. But we live in reality.
Vast areas of pre-farmed arable land exists in Africa, which would benefit from a stable, safe economy. I believe that NGO's could make a difference in these areas before conglomerates get wise. 
We do not have a lack of arable land, or food.
What we cannot sustain, is farming for fuel or the wastage that we get from exported mono-cultured food products.
I realise that your particular ethos involves smallholders, in small co-operatives, where everything is self-sustaining. All well and good, but we also need to apply these techniques to larger co-operatives on a commercial basis. Especially in areas of minimal development. Maybe some small compromises will be necessary (knowing mankind), but I think it could be done better with re-learnt techniques rather than newer ones. But the test must always be that it works best.

As we appear to be on the brink of a global food crisis &lt;snip&gt; Given that we appear to be on the brink of a global food crisis &lt;snip&gt;

There's no one recipe for how a farm should be run and whether it should be big or small. Farms need to be run according to the local customs, traditions and community. The state of a farm in America is not going to be suitable for a farm in Africa and vice versa.

<question>



Thought of an idea to sell ice cream?



I'm already working full time but need extra cash!!! Can get off my butt and put in the hours. Does anyone know the regulations around setting up an ice cream round and what a van should cost that is kitted out? Do you have to have permission or a licence if you own the van and where would you source the ice cream. I know of a few places you could source it from but is there a reasonable rate/percentage you would expect to pay? for the ice cream? What wouldyou pay for an ice cream by the way?



</question>



<answer from>



stickadi...
Member since: 22 March 2007
Total points: 5364 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



You will need a license and permit from your local council and if you think they will be difficult wait till the local Mafia want their slice.



Source(s):



Real life experience.



</answer>



<answer from>



Rachel_S...
Member since: 09 September 2007
Total points: 15620 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Performing Arts



Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, and Transgendered



</answer from>



<answer>



You'd need to do the legal paperwork to set yourself up as a business (set up a corporation).  I have no idea what it would cost to buy an ice cream truck set up with freezers and so forth; maybe you can find a used one somewhere.  You'd invest money in the corporation to buy the ice cream truck and the truck would be in the corporation's name.

As for licenses and permits to operate an ice cream route, you'd need to check with your local town or municipality. I'm assuming you're British (based on your spelling and vocabulary), I have NO idea what the laws are there, so check with your local authorities.



You'd have to find a local ice cream manufacturer and set up an account with them to buy their products on credit.  There are no rates or percentages.  You buy the ice cream for so much per gallon (or liter or whatever unit of measure) and sell it for so much per cone or cup or scoop or whatever. Its up to you to figure out how much you need to sell your ice cream for in order to cover not only the cost of the ice cream but the cost of owning and operating the truck (gasoline, maintenance, insurance, depreciation, etc), and paying yourself a salary.  Do some research and find out what local ice cream shops and restaurants in your area charge for ice cream.  You might be able to set your prices a bit lower since you don't have all the expenses of maintaining a building and paying multiple employees.



Everything is done through the corporation, recording and tracking the sales revenues, paying the operating expenses of the business, and you pay yourself a salary or wage as the corporation's employee (so you'll have to be sure to pay all legally required payroll taxes like Social Security and so on).  The idea is that at the end of the year, the corporation's legitimate expenses should more or less equal the income, so that there is little or no profit to report and pay corporate income taxes on.



Of course, you as the corporation's employee would be responsible for paying personal income tax on your earnings as an ice cream sales person.



Source(s):



accountant for small businesses for 28 years



</answer>

<answer>



It's good to care about this, because nobody should want to cause undue suffering and death to any form of life in this world.  Our survival depends on all sorts of living things, from plants and animals to bugs and bacteria.  The whole biosphere deserves our nurturing and respect.

First, come to terms with the life you've received: human biology is equipped to be an omnivore (e.g. eyes in front of the face, teeth for eating both plant and meat).  It's consistent with human nature to eat meat, and many anthropologists credit a diet rich in animal fats for the development of sophisticated frontal lobes in the brains of early hominids.

That said, it IS possible to buy meat from animals that are raised and killed in ways less-inhumane than factory farms.  Whole-foods markets and specialty meats outlets can help you find what's right for you.  (I've seen cage-free, range-fed, organically-raised meat and dairy products in some local stores.)



</answer>

<question>



Tiger Bread - what is the substance that is put on top of the bread to make it tiger bread?



usually sold in Asda and Tesco



</question>



<answer from>



phoenix2...
Member since: 18 January 2007
Total points: 9967 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



London



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Mmmm... I love tiger bread!
The topping is a paste made of rice flour and water, painted on with a brush after the bread has risen and just before it goes into the oven. 
The heat of the oven makes the paste dry out and also causes the bread to rise a little more. That's why the crust separates into that lovely crackly pattern.



Tiger bread's yummy flavour comes from sesame oil, which is mixed into the dough with the flour, water, yeast and sugar. Most bread has some fat in the dough mix -- olive oil in ciabatta, for instance, and butter in breakfast rolls. It gives it flavour and helps it keep better.



Aargh: no way of buying tiger bread now till tomorrow morning. *whimpers* ;D



</answer>

<answer>



They both have alot of preservatives in them.  It would depend what type of ham you get, but usually you can find very lean ham, so I'd say ham.  Black Forest ham would probably be the very healthiest too, although a genuine Honey Baked Ham (from a Honey Baked store) is absolutely the best tasting!



You should also be able to find turkey pastrami at the deli, and it's very good



</answer>

Dinner protein and salad or vegies...avoid heavy carbs like pasta, rice, etc.

Hope I helped!!!

The key is to watch what you snack on...I like vegies with dips, rice crackers, fruit etc.



</answer>

<answer>



Eat a good breakfast if you're active early in the morning and right into the day. Breakfast should include a whole grain food like oatmeal. Eggs are ok. Wholewheat or multigrain bread is preferable. Include unsweetened orange juice if available. If you're inactive early in the day, a cup of hot tea and some crackers with peanut butter or a small bowl of oatmeal should be enough. Lunch should include a healthy portion of salad alongside the typical hot lunchtime meal. Add fruit as often as possible. Keep a rather modest to low calorie dinner with low carbs and fats, since this is your last meal and you add weight mostly while sleeping. And try not to eat for 2 hours before bedtime. Some exercise will also be necessary; good dieting is never enough. Keep it simple, go for a walk twenty minutes every day. Don't include stopping to talk in the 20 minutes! Best wishes.



</answer>



<answer from>



v´¯)--» L ♥ v e
Member since: 18 July 2008

<answer>



Keep up some regular exercise and try to follow this routine as best you can:

In the morning have a substantial breakfast: either Cereal or a Boiled Egg, Beans, Toast and Fruit Juice.

Allow that to settle and digest, for about 2 hours, then go to the gym, do some jogging, swimming, push-ups, sit-ups, cycling, anything physical, but in general have a good work-out then go and have lunch. Preferably something healthy and fairly light. Either a salad, fruit or sandwich.

After that, you can rest for awhile however, if you're really determined to get fit, do something constructive. Perhaps you can go for a walk around the block, and once that is done, have a good dinner. Preferably a variety of veges and some meat for protein. Try to avoid baked, fried and high cholestrole dinners. Another night you could boiled rice and a stir fry, but if you want sauce in your stir fry make sure it has no MSG.



Just remember, "no snacking on sweets and chocolate." This just makes all your hard effort disappear into thin air.

Hope it helps!

-Angel

<question>



What do Hershey's Candy Corn Kisses taste like?



The taste is so specifically familiar, but I can't place it! It's not candy corn, that' s for sure. It's delicious! is it white chocolate? 
It brought up this vivid memory of a tiny town fair I went to as a kid, which I'd forgotten about. Weird. 
So far I'm about half and half: people who like them and people who don't.
What do you think?



</question>



<answer from>



v´¯)--» L ♥ v e
Member since: 18 July 2008
Total points: 449 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



I must admit, they’re lovely. The wrappers are silver, yellow and orange with little flags that say Candy Corn.



Upon opening the bag I can only say that they stink to high heaven, like fake butter flavor!

Unwrapping the foil, they are super-cute layers just like candy corn. Wider on the bottom than normal candy corn, the proportions may be a little squat, the colors are also rearranged, with yellow on the bottom and orange in the middle, instead of the reverse. I can see why they did it though, it is a pleasant combo.



While I enjoy candy corn that has a slight honey or caramelized sugar taste to it, these go for the buttered corn flavor. I know that the Buttered Popcorn Jelly Belly is one of the most popular, but it’s never floated by boat. Same with this one ... a little caramely white chocolate would have made me very happy. This doesn’t. The fake butter just turns my stomach when I smell it. If I don’t smell it, then they’re not bad, not too sweet with a light little hit of salt.



Unlike many of the other white confection offerings from Hershey’s, these are not white chocolate (which has a cocoa butter base). The ingredients go like this:



Sugar, Vegetable Oil (Palm, Shea, Sunflower and/or Safflower Oil), Nonfat Milk, Lactose, Reduced Minerals Whey (from milk), Milkfat. Contains less than 2% or less of Natural and Artificial Color (Yellow 6, Yellow 5 Lake), Soy Lecithin, PGPR, Tocopherols (to maintain freshness).



I think the idea is cute and I could actually see these being a great cookie decoration (as suggested on the package with a peanut butter cookie recipe). Other than that, I’m going to just admire the photos and the idea and keep the package way from me. I couldn’t decide what rating to give this, mostly because my personal revulsion to fake butter flavor (it actually gives me a headache when someone makes microwave popcorn) is, well, a personal thing. The product is well executed ... I just wish they called them Butter Kisses and made them like real candy corn, not that Milk Maid Caramel Candy Corn. My nose said give them a two out of ten. But looking at the photos, I can’t help but bump it up to a four out of ten ... what can I say, I’m a sucker for design!



Click this link! *(YUMMY MEMORIES)* LOL.

http://images.teamsugar.com/files/users/...

Hope it helps!

-Angel x



</answer>

<answer>



I buy the spiral ham from Costco but they have them at any market.....make sure it is bone in..NOT HONEY  glazed

I also do not use the glaze that comes with it....

I bake my ham with Colemans mustard & brown sugar..

AFTER I take it out of the oven I heat up cherry jelly or blackberry jam(actually you can use any flavor...I add 1 TBSP sugar and bring it to a boil...
I pour it over the ham very slowly...it hardens into a shiny glaze....sprinkle with a little finely chopped parsley and it is very pretty.

Any brand of ham will do Farmer John's is a good brand...but even the Kirkland brand from costco tastes great..

And please do not buy canned ham....fatty & nasty.

yes just a posh name

<answer from>



mom15472...
Member since: 05 May 2007
Total points: 548 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Scallions and green onions generally refer to exactly the same vegetable.
With scallions, you’re generally using the attractive green leafy part of the plant (although the white part closer to the root tastes fine as well); it’s only the very bottom inch or so of the root part of the plant that you won’t use for cooking purposes. Still, don’t throw out those nubby remainders – if you pop the roots into a pot of dirt, and give them sunshine and water of course, the scallions will keep growing, and you’ll have access to fresh, free scallions whenever you need them.



Source(s):



http://www.digsmagazine.com/nourish/nour...



</answer>

<question>



What's the difference between Olive Oil and Olive Pomace oil?



I know what olive oil is but what's the other? Is it worth buying as a substitute?



</question>



<answer from>



psunuc
Member since: 11 April 2008
Total points: 7451 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Mathematics



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Pomace is the solid left behind when you remove juice from a vegetable/fruit.  Often there is still significant amounts of juice left behind that you can extract from the Pumace.  If you then extract juice or oil from it you have pumace oil or pumace juice.  In most cases they are labeled the same because there is only minor differences in the oil/juice so you will never know.



Source(s):



Engineer in the Agriculture Business



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Succinct, informative and helpful. I think I may convert, though according to the other contributor it is blended with another oil after. Still, many thanks for your knowledge.



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



frnkbarr...
Member since: 05 May 2007
Total points: 261 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



I recently asked my local store about pomace. They told me Pomace is good for cooking, and it is. Ordinary olive oil tends to burn at a lower Temperature. Pomace is also cheaper.



</answer>



<answer from>



David H
Member since: 09 August 2006
Total points: 49677 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Cooking & Recipes



Ethnic Cuisine



Other - Food & Drink



</answer from>



<answer>



The second fellow has it surrounded, I ama former chef and toured a Olive Oil production plant in France, it is as he said the reminance of the Olive oil process, they take that mash and introduce a neutral oil, in Europe, soya, safflower or groundnut oil and agitate the mix as it settle the oils combine and it is syphoned off and the remaining mash is sold to farmer for livestock, like pigs and cattle, it is rich in iron and nutrients, I have had real kobe beef in Japan and they feed the cattle sake mash, give it gin massages and rub downs before they end up on the dinner table.



</answer>

<answer>



I guess we're talking about alcohol here. I like Bazooka Joe shots: Shot of 99 Bananas with a splash of grenadine floating on top. Drop in a glass filled with Red Bull and shoot it down. Really tastes just like bubble gum.



I also like Lemon Drops, which are fairly common: Shot of Absolut Cintron (you can also use any lemon-flavored vodka or straight vodka), with a sugared lemon wedge on the side. Shoot the vodka and follow immediately with a bite from the lemon wedge.



Bloody Marys are also lovely and you can find a recipe for them anywhere so I won't bother posting one here. I like to substitute a dill pickle spear for the celery stalk, omit the olives and rim the glass with margarita salt.



</answer>

<question from>



kldr@sbc...
Member since: 05 April 2006
Total points: 2127 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



Food that turns to sugar?



I need to know what food turn into sugar, any and all Please



</question>



<answer from>



Apples to Apples
Member since: 21 September 2006
Total points: 15703 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Cooking & Recipes



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Carbohydrates are foods that turn to sugar inside the body. The carbohydrates that create the highest amount of sugar very quickly are called high glycemic and are sugar and carbohydrates such as bread, pasta, potato, and rice. Other foods such as vegetables (apart from potatoes), nuts and lentils turn to sugar very slowly and are called low glycemic.



Source(s):



http://www.naturalnews.com/023343.html



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Thanks Everyone



</asker's comment>

Mca8
Member since: 03 May 2008
Total points: 299 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>

</answer>



<answer from>



G*G*
Member since: 24 March 2006
Total points: 4647 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>

What are some reasons why all junk food should have health warnings?

melody

</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



So that people know what they are putting in their stomachs as some additives and preservatives can cause some side effects. Also, so that people will know that junk food is not healthy at all as it can cause obesity and if it is salty, it can cause hypertension  or if it is very sweet, it can cause diabetis.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



,



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



Dottie R
Member since: 26 May 2007
Total points: 20975 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Drama



Cooking & Recipes



</answer from>



<answer>



I don't think all "Junk food" should have health warnings.  They already have nutrition labels and people need to learn how to read them for themselves.  Health warnings change often.  For example, sometimes eggs are bad for you and now (at least the last I heard) eggs are ok again.  The FDA approves health warnings for packaging and wouldn't be able to keep up with the changes that the scientific world issues.



And don't forget that we consumers pay for all this labeling.  People need to educate themselves and not rely on health warnings on food products.



</answer>

<answer from>

Contributing In:



Cooking & Recipes



</answer from>



<answer>
