I hope this helps.



</answer>



<answer from>



carm
Member since: 12 July 2006
Total points: 138 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Hot Chocolate S'mores Cookies
adapted from Land O Lakes, found at novice-baker.blogspot.com
1 3/4 cups all-purpose flour
1 cup instant hot chocolate mix [any flavor works, but dark chocolate has been my favorite]
1 teaspoon baking soda
1/2 teaspoon salt
12 tablespoons unsalted butter, softened
1/2 cup granulated sugar
2 large eggs
1/4 cup milk
1 teaspoon vanilla
about 24 marshmallows, cut in half crosswise
about 3 full graham cracker rectangles [I hope that makes sense]



Preheat oven to 350 degrees Fahrenheit.
In a medium bowl, whisk together flour, cocoa mix, baking soda, and salt.
In a large mixing bowl, beat together the butter and sugar until creamy. Add the eggs one at a time and mix until well combined after each. Mix in milk and vanilla. Add the dry ingredients and mix just until combined.
Using a teaspoon or a teaspoon cookie scoop, drop the dough onto parchment lined baking sheets. Bake until the cookies are set [when touched lightly, and indentation remains and the cookie does not spring back], about 7 or 8 minutes. Remove and carefully place a marshmallow, cut side down, in the center of each cookie. I ended up cutting both ends of the marshmallows and then cutting down the middle, which provided me with a sticky surface for my graham cracker crumbs. If using the cracker crumbs, sprinkle on top of the marshmallow halves after placing them on cookies. Place back in the oven and keep baking until marshmallow begins to look puffy [about 1 to 2 minutes]. Remove from oven and let cookies sit on the cookie sheet for 1 minute before removing to cooling racks.



you can also use it for arts and crafts if you have kids... dirt/sand on a picture or fuzzy hair on a person.



</answer>



<answer from>



Lynnie
Member since: 15 October 2007
Total points: 3417 (Level 4)

<answer from>



Cool Hal
Member since: 01 June 2006
Total points: 3708 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



It would be 3 of your 5 DIFFERENT a day.



1 Pineapple counts as 1
1 Mango counts as 1



1 Orange juice, 1 apple juice and 1 grape juice combined count as 1



Although you are eating more than 5 portions of fruit or vegetables you are only eating 3 different.



My advice to you would be to cut down on the quantity and increase the variety.



So try something like



1 Orange Juice = 1 portion
2 slices of pineapple = 1 portion
2 slices of melon = 1 portion



1 apple = 1 portion



1 hand full of grapes = 1 portion.



You have eaten/drank something similar to your original list but hit the requirements of the 5 a day.



Also try and vary it so you may eat this one day but have more vegetable another day.  A general good idea is the more colours the better.



</answer>

<answer from>



Nia G
Member since: 30 October 2008
Total points: 103 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Candy corn is a confection popular in the United States, particularly around Halloween. Created in the 1880s by George Renninger of the Wunderlee Candy Co., the three colors of the candy are meant to mimic corn. Each piece is approximately the size of a whole kernel of corn, as if it fell off a ripe or dried ear of corn. The candy is usually tri-colored with a yellow base, orange center, and white tip, although the color combinations may vary. The most common variant, called "Indian corn", is white, orange, and brown. Indian corn is sometimes associated with the Thanksgiving holiday.
I can eat my body weight in the little sugar hunks! I prefer the shapes though, also known as mellow-creams... It's a personal preference thing though. My husband thinks they are too sweet, but if they hurt your teeth you may have dental issues to look into. Oh, by the way, you shouldn't post questions when you are too "influenced" to type them properly!



Source(s):



Wiki and me!



</answer>

David R

Contributing In:



Cooking & Recipes

<answer>



Before you begin making the eggs, place them in a bowl of water.  If the egg sinks, it's good.  If it sort of floats vertically, it's starting to go bad (use immediately).  If the egg floats, it's bad, don't use it.



Dave



</answer>



<answer from>



knightwi...
Member since: 17 December 2005
Total points: 3035 (Level 4)



</answer from>



<answer>



The smell will tell, but there is an easier way! Before you crack the egg, put it in a bowl (or cup) of water. If it floats, it is bad. If it sinks it should be all right. You can also check the date on the carton.



</answer>

<question>



What are the fine sources of Vitamin A? Is  there any outsider good source Vitamin A?



What are the sources of Vitamin A? I heared that there is no Vitamin A available in any fruit only our body is making it while we consume such thing? SO what about vitamib tablets? Please help me.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Green and orange vegetables are good sources of Vitamin A (as beta carotene).  You want to stay away from vitamin A supplements because too much can be toxic for your body.  The supplements aren't usually made of much beta carotene, which is the safe form of vitamin A.



</answer>

<answer from>



leigh h
Member since: 17 September 2008
Total points: 1106 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Yes, a couple of times. The key to making a great sausage is that you need to add fat otherwise they come out all dry and nasty.



I love making vegetarian sausages with interesting fillings like smoked potato and cheese (my favourite), courgette, cream cheese, sun-dried tomato and nuts, or curried lentils.



Because I work in the food industry I can buy casings direct from the supplier, but you can also ask your butcher. A nice butcher that makes their own will normally sell you some.



Real casings come in different sizes and you drop them in warm water to soften them before you can use them; for vegetarian sausages I use artificial casings which you can usually get from a butcher selling halaal meats 'cos they're not allowed to use intestine casings for religious reasons.



If you don't have a sausage attachment for your mixer, you can put the filling into a piping bag and pipe it into the casing.



</answer>



<answer from>

Member since: 07 February 2008
Total points: 41695 (Level 7)

<answer from>



me me
Member since: 03 January 2008
Total points: 5271 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



I make my own Lorne sausage (scottish  square) and its fantastic



Mince together equal amounts of fatty pork (belly) and beef (skirts best) [1lb each]
Add fresh white bread crumbs [4 - 6oz]
grated nutmeg - to taste
salt and pepper - to taste
beaten egg [1]
spices of your choice - I use ground corriander and chilli



Combine all ingredients thoroughly, line a loaf tin with cling film and firmly press in mixture, Place in freezer till cold but not frozen, remove from tin and slice 1/2" thick, place a piece of parchment between each slice and freeze.



</answer>

<question>



Whats the difference between a fruit and a vegetable?



</question>



<answer from>



CheddarC...
Member since: 16 October 2008
Total points: 1285 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Fruit:



( noun )



the developed ovary of a seed plant with its contents and accessory parts, as the pea pod, nut, tomato, or pineapple.



the edible part of a plant developed from a flower, with any accessory tissues, as the peach, mulberry, or banana



Vegetable:



( noun )



A plant cultivated for an edible part, such as the root of the beet, the leaf of spinach, or the flower buds of broccoli or cauliflower.



Source(s):



http://www.diffen.com/difference/Fruit_v...



</answer>

<answer>



Too much water can upset your salt balances.  You need things like potassium and sodium to function properly, which drinking too much water will flush out of your system.



Drinking only water isn't really the problem, if you eat healthy, but drinking excessive amounts of water can be a problem.



</answer>

<answer>



As long as you eat fruits, vegetables, meats, grains, and dairy, drinking water won't harm you. It's true that even though water flushes out the bad stuff, it also flushes out the good nutrients, but as long as you replenish with good food, you'll be fine. You might also want to try taking vitamins each day for extra nutrients.



Water can be toxic when a large amount is chugged in a short period of time, or if too much water is consumed in general. You will start to feel light headed and perhaps shaky if you have drinken too much water. If this happens, just sit down and eat and you should be fine. :)



</answer>

<answer>



A lot of water can kill you. Try jumping in the sea, put your head below the water for 4 minutes, and see what happens.



How much water are you drinking? A few glasses over the course of the day, or pints and pints? Excess thirst can be an indication of other health problems. Normal amounts is fine. Water is good for you.



As long as you get the nutrients you need from food you are fine.



Remember that drinking too much (excessive) levels of water also interferes with your salt balance, and makes you more prone to illness.



</answer>

<question>



What is the difference between whole kernel and cracked corn in feed?



</question>



<answer from>



DKNY D
Member since: 24 July 2008
Total points: 1536 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



One is Whole the other is Cracked.



</answer>



<answer from>



john o
Member since: 06 August 2008
Total points: 211 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



jimmy crack corn and i dont care



</answer>



<answer from>



Southern Belle
Member since: 06 February 2006
Total points: 8789 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



There isn't really a difference. Cracked corn is whole corn that has been cracked. I assume it'd be easier for an animal to eat [less chewing].



</answer>



<answer from>



Tio Paco
Member since: 24 November 2006
Total points: 5488 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



With cracked corn, the kernels have been passed through a set of rollers to partially crush them, exposing the insides to the outside.



It makes the malting process easier for making into mash, which is needed for fermenting, the first step in making Bourbon Whiskey.



Thus answering the question by Pinky, to The Brain,
"If Jimmy cracks corn, and nobody cares, why does he keep cracking it?"



NARF!



Source(s):



Father of 4,Grand father of 8



</answer>

<answer>

<answer from>



ianchels...

<answer>

<answer from>



D_@z
Member since: 17 April 2008

<answer>



don't cook it overcook
choose meat really lamb not mutton
if lam is so thaugh, you can give some meat tendersier (papain)

This metode is not purpose to make it cooked but only make surface to be brown

<answer from>



leonard
Member since: 30 July 2006
Total points: 2010 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



Hi there,  there's a few things i have to bring to your attention, allot of Butchers call lamb anything from a day old to 1 and a half  years old, the older the lamb the tougher and the darker the meat,  also any lamb that has grown in (hard country) during a drought  will have tough meat, all ways buy lamb that has a very light pink colour and avoid lean lamb, a milky white fat is what you should all ways be looking for,......... next but not least is the way that you cook meat, believe me you can make the best meat  really tough if you don't know how to cook it,  ....all-ways bring the meat to room Temperature for at least 15 minutes before you grill , fry, BBQ, etc etc,  don't cook lamb well done it dries , shrinks, and gets tough as well , but most of all it looses its natural juices  and flavor,  last of all lamb chops from the neck and shoulder (forequarter) will allways be tougher then chops from the mid and back (loin) and leg area,



enjoy



</answer>

<question>



What does spoiled chicken smell like?



I'm trying to figure out if some chicken nuggets are still good to eat or not.  They smell sweet and I can't tell if its the chicken or the batter they used to make them...maybe they're supposed to smell like that...I don't know.



</question>



<additional details>

</additional details>



<answer from>



JackHole...
Member since: 04 May 2008
Total points: 6149 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Homework Help



Movies



</answer from>



<answer>



If it smells okay, then it's okay to eat.  When something goes bad (things start growing on it or it's covered in bacteria) it will produce an offensive odor.



Source(s):



EDIT:  tempura is supposed to smell sweet.



If you have any doubts, deep fry, oven bake or microwave the nuggets again.



</answer>



<answer from>



saladbar...
Member since: 11 April 2006
Total points: 243 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



There will be no doubt if they are bad -- it will make you want to vomit in the sink after taking a good smell of them.



But, you should also consider how long they have been saved.  They say you shouldn't eat them after 3 days in the refrigerator.



</answer>

<original file>9884.html</original file>

<category>

Other - Food & Drink

<question from>



morgan
Member since: 11 August 2008
Total points: 929 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



Swallowing gum effects?



What are they? I've heard they will stick to your intestines and you'll die earlier or that they'll get stuck in your throat eventually or they just dissolve like any other food or they just get pooped out. Answers?



</question>



<answer from>



Aaaa A
Member since: 19 September 2008
Total points: 354 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



It isn't dangerous



Chewing gum consists of a fibre that can't be digested by our bodies, so, if it's swallowed, apart from the unpleasant texture, it will pass harmlessly through the body intact along with other waste. There is no way it could get lost and wrap itself around vital organs or lurk in the stomach for untold years.



Source(s):



http://www.raisingkids.co.uk/ASK/ex07_pr...



</answer>



<answer from>



You know all you need to know
Member since: 06 March 2007
Total points: 114 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



chewing gum, takes longer to break down, because of the chemical properties but it does break down after maybe 24 hours!



</answer>



<answer from>



Kristen S
Member since: 20 October 2008
Total points: 132 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



they proved it on mythbusters, gum is just like any other food you swallow, it will pass through within 24 hours...



</answer>



<answer from>



The Chosen One
Member since: 31 August 2008
Total points: 2024 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



yeah they tested it on mythbusters (love that show) and watever goes in, must come out!



hehe I swallowed my gum last saturday at the movies



Source(s):



I saw HSM3 :)



</answer>



<answer from>



bobo
Member since: 19 August 2008
Total points: 610 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



ive heard that it takes 7 years to digest a single piece
so



but i dont believe it
i still do it
haha



</answer>



<answer from>



Shannon C
Member since: 06 January 2008
Total points: 458 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



In rare cases, swallowing a large mass of gum, or many small pieces of gum over a short period of time, can block the digestive tract. Blockages in the digestive system are most likely to happen when gum is swallowed along with other indigestible things (like sunflower seed shells).



Although people cannot digest gum resin, they can digest the things that have been added to chewing gum, such as sweeteners or even medications (think of the nicotine gum used by people trying to quit smoking). The body absorbs these just through the act of chewing. This is where chewing gum can affect a person's health: When a person chews a lot of sugary gum, the calories can add up



</answer>
